⏺ Good — I have a clear picture. The project is design-only right now: three
  docs (prompt.md, workflow.md, application.md) describing an LLM-powered wiki
  CLI in Rust, with zero implementation code.

  Before I propose approaches, let me ask my first clarifying question:

  How do you envision this Rust application interacting with the LLM?

  - A) The Rust app handles file processing (PDF splitting, ZIP extraction,
  audio transcription, etc.) and then shells out to an LLM CLI (like claude or
  openai) to do the wiki writing/updating
  - B) The Rust app calls an LLM API directly (Anthropic API, OpenAI API) to
  generate/update wiki pages as part of its pipeline
  - C) The Rust app is purely a file orchestrator — it prepares files for
  ingestion but the actual LLM wiki-building happens in a separate session
  (e.g., you paste results into Claude Code manually)
  - D) Something else?

  This fundamentally shapes the architecture — whether the app is a pipeline
  that includes LLM calls, or a preprocessing tool that feeds an external LLM
  workflow.

✻ Cooked for 1m 5s

❯ I think we should do option A. I am imagining a Rust app that does the        
  preprocessing and extraction and such things. The only problem I can see with 
   that is it's hard to get the LLM to make a choice and/or take an action. If  
  the LLM wanted some action taken by the Rust app, then it would have to send  
  a structured response back for the Rust app to interpret unambiguously.       
                                                                                
  Do you agree? What other ways am I committing to choices very early by doing  
  this?                                                                         
⏺ You're right to flag this — it's the most consequential early decision. Let me
   unpack it.

  The structured response problem is real, but solvable in two ways:

  1. Rust app stays in control (push model). The Rust app makes all
  preprocessing decisions itself — it inspects the PDF, decides it's a book,
  splits chapters, then hands each chunk to the LLM with explicit instructions:
  "Here's chapter 3 of Book X. Write a summary page and tell me which
  entity/concept pages to update." The LLM returns wiki content, and the Rust
  app writes the files. The LLM never needs to request actions because the Rust
  app has already done all the work before asking.

  This works well for the workflow in workflow.md — the decision tree (is it a
  PDF? is it a book? is it sensitive?) is deterministic and doesn't need LLM
  judgment. The LLM's job is content generation, not orchestration.

  2. LLM drives the process (pull model). The LLM decides what to do and
  requests actions. This is the structured-response problem you identified. The
  clean solution here is MCP — your Rust app becomes an MCP server exposing
  tools like split_pdf, extract_zip, write_wiki_page, read_wiki_page,
  update_index. Claude Code (or any MCP-compatible client) connects to it, and
  the LLM orchestrates by calling your tools. No parsing ambiguity — it's native
   tool use.

  What you're committing to early by choosing Option A (shell out to CLI):

  - The Rust app must own all file-type decisions. The LLM can't say "actually,
  this PDF looks like a textbook, split it differently." You'd need to encode
  that heuristic in Rust or accept that the LLM only gets pre-processed output.
  - Stateless LLM calls. Each CLI invocation has no memory of previous
  ingestions. You'd need to feed relevant context (existing wiki pages,
  index.md) into each call's prompt. This gets expensive as the wiki grows.
  - Prompt engineering in Rust. You'll be constructing prompts as strings in
  Rust code. Iterating on prompts means recompiling (or reading them from
  template files).
  - Single LLM provider coupling. Shelling out to claude is different from
  openai. You'd want an abstraction layer, or you're locked in.
  - No contradiction detection across sources. The LLM sees one source at a
  time. Flagging contradictions with existing wiki content requires feeding
  relevant existing pages into each call.

  My recommendation: Consider a hybrid. The Rust app handles preprocessing (ZIP
  extraction, PDF splitting, audio transcription, file-type filtering) — that's
  pure Rust, no LLM needed. But for the wiki-building step, make the Rust app an
   MCP server rather than shelling out. This gives you:

  - The LLM can read existing wiki pages before deciding how to update them
  (solves the stateless problem)
  - Structured tool calls instead of parsing text responses (solves the
  structured response problem)
  - You can use it from Claude Code today, or any future MCP client
  - The Rust app still owns the heavy lifting; the LLM just orchestrates the
  knowledge work

  Does this framing change your thinking? Or do you want to stay with the
  simpler shell-out approach and accept the constraints?

⏺ That's a lot of PDFs. Follow-up question:

  How do you want to handle the initial bulk ingest of ~2000 files?

  - A) Batch unattended — point it at a directory, walk away, review results
  later. Prioritize throughput. Accept that some results may need manual review.
  - B) Supervised batches — ingest in chunks (e.g., 50 at a time), review wiki
  state between batches, adjust as you go.
  - C) One at a time initially — start slow to tune the prompts and wiki
  structure, then switch to batch mode once you're happy with the quality.

  This affects whether we need a job queue, progress tracking, retry logic, and
  how prominent the TUI's monitoring capabilities need to be from day one. With
  2000 files, option A or B likely means we need robust error handling and a way
   to resume interrupted ingestions.

   how to handle ZIP files and whether to split PDFs into multiple chapters.    
  The Rust app maintains a terminal user interface to track the progress --

  For PDF classification — deciding whether a PDF is a book to split, a simple 
  document to ingest whole, or a sensitive file to reject — how much do you want
   the Rust app to decide on its own vs. asking the LLM?

  - A) Rust heuristics first — page count, presence of TOC/bookmarks, filename
  patterns for sensitive docs. Only ask the LLM if ambiguous.
  - B) LLM decides — send the first few pages to the LLM via MCP tool call, let
  it classify. More accurate but costs an API call per file.
  - C) User pre-sorts — you organize files into directories (books/, articles/,
  skip/) before ingesting, and the app trusts the directory structure.

  With 2000 PDFs, option B is ~2000 extra LLM calls just for classification.
  Option A keeps costs down but might misclassify some files.

  - B) API-based — send audio to a transcription API (OpenAI Whisper API,

  - C) Defer this — skip audio/video support for v1. Focus on PDF, markdown,

  Given 2000 PDFs waiting, I'd recommend C — get the core pipeline working first

  sources too, it might be worth including from the start.

  - B) Claude Desktop — same MCP server but connected via Claude Desktop app.

  queue" and it would call your MCP tools. In B, same but through the desktop
  UI. C means we don't bake in assumptions about the client.

❯ What are the implications of deferring this:                                  
  > Query operation (asking questions against the wiki)                         
                                                                                
  I want the wiki to be human-readable **and** I want to Claude to be able to   
  use it for sourcing information.                                              

⏺ Good distinction. If the wiki is Obsidian-native markdown with wikilinks,
  index.md, and frontmatter — it's already queryable by Claude. You don't need a
   special "query" feature in the Rust app for that.

  Here's why: Claude Code can already read files, grep, and glob. If the wiki
  lives in a directory, you can just point Claude Code at it — read index.md to
  find relevant pages, then read those pages. That's the query operation
  described in prompt.md, and it works today with zero code.

  What "query as a feature" would add later:
  - Structured search (BM25/vector) when the wiki is too large for index.md
  scanning
  - Automated context assembly — the Rust app finds relevant pages and bundles
  them into a prompt
  - Filing query results back into the wiki as new pages

  But at hundreds-to-low-thousands of pages, index.md + Claude Code's native
  file tools is sufficient. You lose nothing by deferring the Rust-side query
  feature.

  So the real answer: you're not deferring queryability — you're deferring
  building a search engine. The wiki is queryable from day one because it's just
   markdown files that Claude can read.

  Does that resolve the concern?

⏺ Fair — and your instinct about scale is worth noting. We'll design the wiki
  structure so that adding search later (qmd, tantivy, or similar) is a drop-in,
   not a rearchitect.

  Now let me propose approaches. Here are three ways to structure the Rust
  application:

  ---
  Approach A: Monolithic Binary

  Single Rust binary that is both the CLI/TUI and the MCP server, selected by
  subcommand (app ingest, app tui, app mcp-serve). All file processing logic
  lives in one crate.

  - Pro: Simple to build, deploy, and reason about. One binary, one repo.
  - Con: The MCP server must run as a long-lived process while the TUI is a
  separate interactive process. Coupling them means shared state gets
  complicated. Harder to split work across crates later.

  Approach B: Two Binaries, Shared Library (Recommended)

  A library crate (ai-wiki-core) with all the domain logic — PDF classification,
   ZIP extraction, queue management, wiki file operations. Two thin binary
  crates consume it:

  1. ai-wiki — CLI with ingest and tui subcommands. Manages the queue, drives
  preprocessing, launches the TUI.
  2. ai-wiki-mcp — MCP server exposing tools that Claude Code calls to
  read/write wiki pages, update index, read queue state.

  They share the library but run as separate processes. The queue state lives on
   disk (SQLite or a simple JSON/TOML file) so both can access it.

  - Pro: Clean separation. MCP server is stateless and simple. CLI/TUI handles
  orchestration. Easy to test the library independently. Follows your CLAUDE.md
  guidance about splitting into logical crates.
  - Con: Two binaries to build and coordinate. Need a shared on-disk state
  format.

  Approach C: MCP-Only

  No CLI at all. The Rust app is purely an MCP server. You drive everything
  through Claude Code: "ingest this directory," "show me queue status," "process
   the next file." The TUI is replaced by Claude Code's own output.

  - Pro: Simplest Rust code — just tools. No TUI to build. Claude Code is the
  UI.
  - Con: You lose the standalone TUI for monitoring. Every operation requires
  Claude Code in the loop. Batch processing 2000 files through conversational
  turns would be painful.

  ---
  I recommend Approach B. The library crate keeps logic testable and reusable.
  The two binaries have clearly different lifetimes — the MCP server runs
  persistently while Claude Code is connected, the CLI runs on-demand for queue
  management and monitoring. SQLite for queue state is lightweight and
  battle-tested.

  What's your take?

❯ Approach B.                                                                   

⏺ Good. Let me present the design section by section. I'll keep each focused and
   wait for your approval before moving on.

  ---
  Section 1: Project Structure

  ai-wiki/
  ├── Cargo.toml              # workspace root
  ├── crates/
  │   ├── ai-wiki-core/       # library crate — all domain logic
  │   │   ├── Cargo.toml
  │   │   └── src/
  │   ├── ai-wiki/            # CLI binary — ingest, tui
  │   │   ├── Cargo.toml
  │   │   └── src/
  │   └── ai-wiki-mcp/        # MCP server binary
  │       ├── Cargo.toml
  │       └── src/
  ├── docs/
  │   └── design/             # existing design docs
  ├── raw/                    # immutable source files (user-managed)
  │   └── assets/             # downloaded images
  └── wiki/                   # LLM-generated Obsidian vault
      ├── index.md
      ├── log.md
      ├── entities/
      ├── concepts/
      ├── sources/
      └── .obsidian/          # minimal Obsidian config

  Key decisions:
  - Cargo workspace with three crates, per your CLAUDE.md guidance on splitting
  into logical crates
  - raw/ and wiki/ live in the project root by default but are configurable (so
  you can point at ~/Downloads or an existing Obsidian vault)
  - The wiki directory structure mirrors the page categories that index.md will
  organize by

  Does this structure look right?
❯ Seems fine. Proceed.                                                          

⏺ Section 2: Library Crate (ai-wiki-core)

  This is where all the real logic lives. Four modules:

  queue — Job queue backed by SQLite.
  - Each source file becomes a queue item with status: queued, in_progress,
  complete, rejected, error
  - Stores: file path, file type, status, timestamps, parent item (for ZIP
  contents / PDF chapters), error message if failed
  - Supports resume — on restart, in_progress items reset to queued
  - Both the CLI and MCP server read/write this same database

  preprocessing — File inspection and preparation. No LLM involved.
  - File type detection (by extension + magic bytes)
  - PDF classifier: page count, bookmark/outline extraction via lopdf, metadata
  inspection. Heuristics: has TOC outline + >50 pages = book; filename/metadata
  matching sensitive patterns = reject
  - PDF splitter: extract chapter ranges from bookmarks, split via pdf crate or
  shelling out to qpdf
  - ZIP extractor: unpack, enqueue each contained file as a child item
  - Audio extractor: shell out to ffmpeg to extract audio from MP4/MKV, then to
  whisper-cli for transcription to markdown

  wiki — Wiki file operations. These become MCP tools.
  - Read/write/update markdown pages in the Obsidian vault
  - Manage [[wikilinks]] and YAML frontmatter
  - Append to log.md
  - Read and update index.md
  - Create pages in the right subdirectory (entities/, concepts/, sources/)

  config — Application configuration.
  - Paths to raw/, wiki/, SQLite database
  - PDF classification thresholds
  - Sensitive file patterns to reject
  - Loaded from a TOML config file with sensible defaults

  Does this module breakdown make sense?

❯ Yes, that is fine.                                                            

⏺ Section 3: CLI Binary (ai-wiki)

  Two subcommands via clap:

  ai-wiki ingest <path>
  - <path> can be a file, a glob, or a directory
  - Walks the path, runs preprocessing on each file (classify, split, extract),
  enqueues items into SQLite
  - For compound files (ZIP, book PDFs), enqueues child items linked to the
  parent
  - Does not call the LLM — it only prepares the queue. The LLM-driven wiki
  writing happens through the MCP server when Claude Code processes queue items.
  - Prints a summary: N items queued, N rejected, N errors

  ai-wiki tui
  - Launches a terminal UI (via ratatui) showing the queue
  - Columns: filename, type, status, started at, parent item
  - Expandable rows for compound items (ZIP contents, book chapters)
  - Color-coded status: gray=queued, yellow=in-progress, green=complete,
  red=rejected/error
  - Auto-refreshes by polling SQLite
  - Read-only view — it monitors, doesn't modify

  The key insight: ingest is fast and offline. You can run ai-wiki ingest 
  ~/Downloads/*.pdf and it classifies and queues 2000 files in seconds. The slow
   part — LLM wiki generation — happens separately through Claude Code calling
  the MCP server, and you watch progress in the TUI.

  Does this feel right for the CLI?

❯ yes.                                                                          

⏺ Section 4: MCP Server (ai-wiki-mcp)

  A long-running process that Claude Code connects to via claude mcp add.
  Exposes tools that let the LLM drive the wiki-building step.

  Queue tools:
  - get_next_item — returns the next queued item (path, file type, parent info),
   marks it in_progress
  - complete_item(id) — marks an item complete
  - reject_item(id, reason) — marks an item rejected with explanation
  - error_item(id, message) — marks an item error
  - list_items(status?) — list queue items, optionally filtered by status

  Source tools:
  - read_source(id) — reads the preprocessed source file content. For PDFs,
  returns extracted text. For markdown, returns the file contents.

  Wiki tools:
  - read_page(path) — read an existing wiki page
  - write_page(path, content) — create or overwrite a wiki page (markdown with
  frontmatter and wikilinks)
  - list_pages(directory?) — list pages, optionally within a subdirectory
  - read_index — read current index.md
  - update_index(entry) — add or update an entry in index.md
  - append_log(entry) — append a timestamped entry to log.md

  The workflow from Claude Code's perspective:
  1. Call get_next_item — gets a source to process
  2. Call read_source — reads its content
  3. Call read_index + relevant read_page calls — understands existing wiki
  state
  4. Generates wiki content (summaries, entity updates, concept pages)
  5. Calls write_page for each page created/updated
  6. Calls update_index and append_log
  7. Calls complete_item
  8. Repeat

  The LLM orchestrates; the Rust app does the I/O. Does this tool surface look
  right?

❯ yes.                                                                          

⏺ Section 5: PDF Text Extraction

  One thing I glossed over — read_source needs to return text content from PDFs.
   The preprocessing step classifies and splits, but we also need to extract
  readable text.

  Approach: Use pdf-extract or lopdf for text extraction at read time. For PDFs
  with scanned images (no embedded text), fall back to OCR — shell out to
  tesseract which is available via Homebrew on macOS.

  - Simple PDFs with embedded text: extract directly, fast
  - Scanned PDFs: OCR via tesseract, slower but handles the common case
  - The preprocessing step can flag which PDFs need OCR (no extractable text) so
   the TUI shows this

  This means two external tool dependencies: tesseract for OCR and qpdf for PDF
  splitting. Both available via brew install.

  Acceptable, or would you prefer to avoid external dependencies?

❯ acceptable                                                                    

⏺ Section 6: Error Handling and Resilience

  With 2000 files, things will fail. The design needs to handle this gracefully.

  Queue resilience:
  - SQLite gives us ACID transactions — no corrupted state on crash
  - On restart, any in_progress items reset to queued for retry
  - Items that fail repeatedly (e.g., corrupted PDF) get marked error with the
  failure message, and processing continues to the next item

  MCP server failures:
  - Each tool call is independent — if Claude Code disconnects mid-ingestion,
  the current item stays in_progress and gets retried on reconnect
  - No in-memory state beyond what's in SQLite

  Preprocessing failures:
  - A bad ZIP, unreadable PDF, or failed transcription marks that item as error
  and continues
  - Child items of a failed parent are not enqueued

  No retry loops or exponential backoff. If something fails, it's marked error
  and skipped. You can review errors in the TUI and re-queue manually if you
  want. Keeps the design simple.

  Does this approach to failure handling work for you?

❯ sounds good                                                                   

⏺ Section 7: Key Dependencies

  Rust crates:
  - clap — CLI argument parsing
  - ratatui + crossterm — TUI
  - rusqlite — SQLite access
  - lopdf — PDF inspection (bookmarks, page count, metadata)
  - pdf-extract — PDF text extraction
  - rmcp — Rust MCP SDK for building the server
  - serde + toml — config file parsing
  - zip — ZIP file extraction
  - chrono — timestamps for log entries

  External tools (installed separately):
  - qpdf — PDF splitting by page range
  - tesseract — OCR for scanned PDFs
  - ffmpeg — audio extraction from video files
  - whisper-cli — audio transcription (deferred to post-MVP but architecture
  supports it)

  That's the full design. To summarize the whole picture:

  - Cargo workspace with three crates: core library, CLI binary, MCP server
  binary
  - CLI preprocesses files (classify, split, extract) and enqueues them in
  SQLite
  - TUI monitors queue progress in real time
  - MCP server exposes queue and wiki tools for Claude Code to drive the
  wiki-building
  - Obsidian-native wiki output with wikilinks, frontmatter, index.md, log.md
  - Resilient — crash-safe queue, skip-on-error, resume on restart

  Does the overall design look good to proceed to writing the spec document?

❯ Looks good. Proceed.

  that runs locally and works well on Apple Silicon with Metal acceleration.

           +` for the tool impl block, `Parameters<T>` wrapper structs wi
           +th `schemars::JsonSchema` for tool parameters, and `rmcp::tra
           +nsport::stdio` for the transport. The implementer MUST verify
           + the exact API against `rmcp` 1.x docs/examples at build time
           +, as macro-based APIs are fragile across minor versions. The 
           +code below reflects the best-known API as of writing; adjust 
           +if `cargo check` reveals differences.

      113 +    fn default_claude_md() -> String {                        
      114 +        r#"# AI Wiki Schema                                   
      115 +                                                              
      116 +## Wiki Structure                                             
      117 +                                                              
      118 +This is an Obsidian-native wiki maintained by an LLM via MCP t
          +ools.                                                         
      119 +                                                              
      120 +### Directories                                               
      121 +- `entities/` — People, places, organizations                 
      122 +- `concepts/` — Ideas, themes, theories                       
      123 +- `claims/` — Specific assertions from sources (tag data point
          +s with `data-point: true`)                                    
      124 +- `sources/` — Summaries of ingested source files             
      125 +                                                              
      126 +### Page Format                                               
      127 +                                                              
      128 +Every page must have YAML frontmatter:                        
      129 +                                                              
      130 +```yaml                                                       
      131 +---                                                           
      132 +type: entity | concept | claim | source                       
      133 +tags: [relevant, tags]                                        
      134 +sources: [source-filename.pdf]                                
      135 +created: YYYY-MM-DD                                           
      136 +updated: YYYY-MM-DD                                           
      137 +data-point: true  # only for claims that are data points      
      138 +contradicted: true  # only if contradicted by another source  
      139 +---                                                           
      140 +```                                                           
      141 +                                                              
      142 +Use `[[wikilinks]]` for all cross-references between pages.   
      143 +                                                              
      144 +### Contradictions                                            
      145 +                                                              
      146 +When a new source contradicts an existing claim or page, add a
          + callout:                                                     
      147 +                                                              
      148 +```markdown                                                   
      149 +> [!warning] Contradiction                                    
      150 +> Source A claims X, but Source B (this source) claims Y.     
      151 +```                                                           
      152 +                                                              
      153 +Tag the page with `contradicted: true` in frontmatter.        
      154 +                                                              
      155 +### Ingestion Workflow                                        
      156 +                                                              
      157 +For each source item from the queue:                          
      158 +                                                              
      159 +1. Call `get_next_item` to receive the next source            
      160 +2. Call `read_source` to read the preprocessed text           
      161 +3. Call `read_index` to understand what exists in the wiki    
      162 +4. Read relevant existing pages with `read_page`              
      163 +5. Extract entities, concepts, claims, and data points        
      164 +6. Create or update wiki pages with `write_page`              
      165 +7. Update cross-references using `[[wikilinks]]`              
      166 +8. Flag any contradictions with existing content              
      167 +9. Call `update_index` for each new page                      
      168 +10. Call `append_log` with a summary of what was ingested     
      169 +11. Call `complete_item` with the primary wiki page path      
      170 +                                                              
      171 +### Index Format                                              
      172 +                                                              
      173 +Entries in index.md follow this format:                       
      174 +```                                                           
      175 +- [[directory/page-name]] — One-line summary                  
      176 +```                                                           
      177 +                                                              
      178 +Organized under section headings: ## Entities, ## Concepts, ##
          + Claims, ## Sources                                           
      179 +                                                              
      180 +### Log Format                                                
      181 +                                                              
      182 +Each log entry is prefixed: `## [YYYY-MM-DD] action | Title`  
      183 +                                                              
      184 +Actions: `ingest`, `update`, `query`, `lint`                  
      185 +"#.to_string()

  Key capabilities:
  - Ingest: ai-wiki ingest <path> — classifies files, splits PDFs, extracts
  ZIPs, queues everything in SQLite
  - TUI: ai-wiki tui — real-time color-coded queue monitor
  - MCP Server: 12 tools (queue management, source reading, wiki CRUD) for
  Claude Code to drive wiki building

  To start using it:
  # Ingest files
  cargo run -p ai-wiki -- ingest ~/Downloads/*.pdf

  # Monitor progress
  cargo run -p ai-wiki -- tui

  # Register MCP server with Claude Code
  claude mcp add ai-wiki -- cargo run --manifest-path /path/to/Cargo.toml -p

      360      Ok(())

      363 +fn read_file_list(list_path: &str) -> anyhow::Result<Vec<PathB
          +uf>> {                                                        
      364 +    let content = fs::read_to_string(list_path)               
      365 +        .with_context(|| format!("failed to read file list: {l
          +ist_path}"))?;                                                
      366 +                                                              
      367 +    let files: Vec<PathBuf> = content                         
      368 +        .lines()                                              
      369 +        .map(|line| line.trim())                              
      370 +        .filter(|line| !line.is_empty() && !line.starts_with('
          +#'))                                                          
      371 +        .map(PathBuf::from)                                   
      372 +        .collect();                                           
      373 +                                                              
      374 +    if files.is_empty() {                                     
      375 +        anyhow::bail!("file list is empty: {list_path}");     
      376 +    }                                                         
      377 +                                                              
      378 +    // Verify all listed files exist                          
      379 +    let mut missing = Vec::new();                             
      380 +    for f in &files {                                         
      381 +        if !f.is_file() {                                     
      382 +            missing.push(f.display().to_string());            
      383 +        }                                                     
      384 +    }                                                         
      385 +    if !missing.is_empty() {                                  
      386 +        anyhow::bail!(                                        
      387 +            "{} file(s) from list not found: {}",             
      388 +            missing.len(),                                    
      389 +            missing.join(", ")                                
      390 +        );                                                    
      391 +    }                                                         
      392 +                                                              
      393 +    Ok(files)                                                 
      394 +}                                                             
      395 +

           ───────────────────

⏺ The UNIQUE index doesn't work because parent_id IS NULL for both inserts, and
  SQLite treats NULL as distinct for UNIQUE constraints. I need to use a
  different approach — use a sentinel value (0) instead of NULL, or use a
  partial index. The simpler approach: change the UNIQUE index to use COALESCE:

❯ How do I run this to see the data as a wiki?                                  

⏺ Here's the end-to-end workflow:

  1. Install external tools

  brew install qpdf poppler tesseract

  2. Set up your config

  Create ai-wiki.toml in your working directory (or it gets auto-created with
  defaults):

  [paths]
  raw_dir = "/Users/hughbrown/workspace/hughdbrown/rust/ai-wiki/raw"
  wiki_dir = "/Users/hughbrown/workspace/hughdbrown/rust/ai-wiki/wiki"
  database_path =
  "/Users/hughbrown/workspace/hughdbrown/rust/ai-wiki/ai-wiki.db"
  processed_dir = "/Users/hughbrown/workspace/hughdbrown/rust/ai-wiki/processed"

  3. Ingest source files

  # Single file
  cargo run -p ai-wiki -- ingest ~/Downloads/some-article.pdf

  # All PDFs
  cargo run -p ai-wiki -- ingest "~/Downloads/*.pdf"

  # From a file list
  cargo run -p ai-wiki -- ingest @my-files.txt

  This classifies, splits, and extracts text — but does NOT build wiki pages
  yet. It just prepares the queue.

  4. Register the MCP server with Claude Code

  claude mcp add ai-wiki -- cargo run --manifest-path
  /Users/hughbrown/workspace/hughdbrown/rust/ai-wiki/Cargo.toml -p ai-wiki-mcp

  This tells Claude Code about the 12 MCP tools. You only do this once.

  5. Open the wiki directory in Obsidian

  Open Obsidian, click "Open folder as vault", select:
  /Users/hughbrown/workspace/hughdbrown/rust/ai-wiki/wiki/

  You'll see the initial structure: entities/, concepts/, claims/, sources/,
  plus index.md, log.md, and CLAUDE.md.

  6. Tell Claude Code to process the queue

  In a Claude Code session, say something like:

  ▎ Process the next source from the ai-wiki queue. Read it, extract key 
  ▎ entities, concepts, and claims, create wiki pages with proper frontmatter 
  ▎ and wikilinks, update the index, and log what you did.

  Claude Code will use the MCP tools:
  1. get_next_item — picks up the next queued file
  2. read_source — reads the extracted text
  3. read_index — sees what's already in the wiki
  4. write_page — creates pages in entities/, concepts/, sources/
  5. update_index — adds entries to index.md
  6. append_log — records what was ingested
  7. complete_item — marks the queue item done

  To process multiple items:

  ▎ Process the next 5 items from the ai-wiki queue, one at a time.

  7. Monitor progress in the TUI

  In a separate terminal:
  cargo run -p ai-wiki -- tui

  This shows a live table of queue items with color-coded status. Press q to
  quit, r to refresh.

  8. Browse in Obsidian

  As Claude Code writes wiki pages, Obsidian auto-refreshes. You'll see:
  - Pages appearing in entities/, concepts/, claims/, sources/
  - [[wikilinks]] connecting pages
  - Graph view showing the knowledge network growing
  - index.md cataloging everything
  - log.md showing the ingestion timeline

  ---
  The key insight: The Rust app handles preprocessing (the grunt work). Claude
  Code handles the intelligence (reading, understanding, writing wiki pages).
  Obsidian is the viewer. You're the curator.

⏺ First 10 items processed — 10 source pages, 18 concept pages, 8 entity pages,
  7 claim pages created. Now let me fix the TUI error.

  The error "Conversion error from type Text at index: 0, premature end of
  input" means the SQLite database has a row with an invalid/empty timestamp
  that row_to_item can't parse. Likely caused by the manual sqlite3 UPDATE
  commands I used (which used datetime('now') instead of RFC3339 format).

⏺ Bash(sqlite3 /Users/hughbrown/workspace/hughdbrown/rust/ai-wiki/ai-wiki.db
      "SELECT id, status, created_at, started_at, completed_at FROM queue_items
      WHERE created_at…)

     4-10 02:34:17
     2|complete|2026-04-10T02:03:18.123420+00:00|2026-04-10 02:37:24|2026-0
     … +7 lines (ctrl+o to expand)

⏺ There it is. created_at is RFC3339 (2026-04-10T02:03:15.888143+00:00) but
  started_at and completed_at are SQLite datetime('now') format (2026-04-10 
  02:31:50) — missing the T separator and timezone. The Rust parser expects
  RFC3339.

  Two fixes needed: (1) make the parser more tolerant, and (2) fix the bad data.

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

  make it tolerate the SQLite datetime() format too.

      278 +    pub fn requeue_item(&self, id: i64) -> Result<(), QueueErr
          +or> {                                                         
      279 +        let rows = self.conn.execute(                         
      280 +            "UPDATE queue_items SET status = ?1, started_at =

      286 +            ],                                                
      287 +        )?;

      289 +            return Err(self.not_found_or_transition(id, "error

⏺ Here's what pdf-dump revealed about the three books:

  Findings

  Bug in split_pdf_chapters: The current code uses ALL outline Destination
  entries for splitting, including sub-sections (level 2, 3, etc.). It should
  only use top-level (level 1) entries.

  ┌──────────────────┬───────┬─────────┬──────────┬────────────────────────┐
  │       Book       │ Pages │  TOC    │ Current  │ Correct splits (level  │
  │                  │       │ Entries │  splits  │        1 only)         │
  ├──────────────────┼───────┼─────────┼──────────┼────────────────────────┤
  │                  │       │         │          │ 7 (but outlines are    │
  │ Web Dev on       │ 187   │ 7       │ 7        │ only front matter —    │
  │ Netlify          │       │         │          │ real chapters not      │
  │                  │       │         │          │ bookmarked)            │
  ├──────────────────┼───────┼─────────┼──────────┼────────────────────────┤
  │ 30 Agents        │ 542   │ 491     │ 315      │ 98                     │
  │ (9781806109012)  │       │         │          │                        │
  ├──────────────────┼───────┼─────────┼──────────┼────────────────────────┤
  │ Context          │ 394   │ 317     │ 229      │ 78                     │
  │ Engineering      │       │         │          │                        │
  └──────────────────┴───────┴─────────┴──────────┴────────────────────────┘

  Two separate problems:

  1. Over-splitting: split_pdf_chapters splits on every sub-section, not just
  chapters. The fix: use doc.get_toc() and filter to level == 1 entries only.
  2. Netlify book: Its outlines only contain front matter bookmarks (Cover,
  Title Page, TOC, etc.), not actual chapter bookmarks. The entire book content
  (pages 8-182) ends up as one block labeled "Table of Contents." This is a
  publisher/PDF issue, not our code — the bookmarks are just incomplete.

  Want me to fix the splitting code to use level-1-only entries from get_toc()?

⏺ Done. The new command:

  # Process 10 items (default)
  ai-wiki process

  # Process a larger batch
  ai-wiki process --batch 50

  # Via justfile
  just process 50

  It launches claude --print --dangerously-skip-permissions with a detailed
  prompt that tells Claude to:
  1. Claim items from the SQLite queue
  2. Read extracted text from processed/{id}.txt
  3. Create wiki pages with proper frontmatter and wikilinks
  4. Handle book parents by reading their children's text
  5. Update index.md and log.md
  6. Print [N/batch] filename ... done (created X pages) progress
  7. Mark items complete in the database

⏺ Write(README.md)
  ⎿  Wrote 275 lines to README.md
      1 # ai-wiki
      2 
      3 A Rust application that builds and maintains a personal knowledge
         base by having an LLM incrementally process your documents into 
        an interlinked Obsidian wiki.
      4 
      5 ## What is this?
      6 
      7 Most people's experience with LLMs and documents looks like RAG: 
        upload files, retrieve chunks at query time, generate an answer. 
        The LLM rediscovers knowledge from scratch on every question. Not
        hing accumulates.
      8 
      9 ai-wiki takes a different approach. Instead of retrieving from ra
        w documents at query time, the LLM **incrementally builds and mai
        ntains a persistent wiki** -- a structured collection of markdown
         files that sits between you and your sources. When you add a new
         document, the LLM reads it, extracts the key information, and in
        tegrates it into the existing wiki: updating entity pages, creati
        ng concept pages, noting claims and data points, cross-referencin
        g everything with `[[wikilinks]]`. The knowledge is compiled once
         and kept current, not re-derived on every query.
     … +265 lines (ctrl+o to expand)

✻ Crunched for 2m 32s

❯ If there is a `ai-wiki process`, then there should be a verb to re-run the    
  errors (with the belief that they will turn out differently).                 
                                                                                
  Or maybe just clear the errors and drop the books that did not process? Not   
  sure. Tell me your view.                                                      

⏺ There are two kinds of errors in the queue:

  1. Text extraction failures (the majority) — PDFs where pdf-extract panicked
  or pdftotext wasn't installed at ingest time. These are fixable: re-ingest
  with the tools now installed and the text will extract fine. Requeuing these
  for process would fail the same way because the processed text file still
  doesn't exist.

  2. Processing failures — items that have processed text but Claude failed to
  create wiki pages (timeout, network error, etc.). These are genuinely
  retryable.

  So "retry errors" is really two different operations:

  - ai-wiki reingest — re-extract text for items that failed during ingest
  (needs to re-run the PDF pipeline, not just requeue)
  - ai-wiki retry — requeue items that have processed text but failed during the
   wiki-building phase

  My recommendation: add ai-wiki retry for case 2 (it just resets errored items
  to queued, then runs process). For case 1, the user should delete the errored
  items and re-ingest the original files — which is what ai-wiki ingest already
  does if you point it at the same files again.

  But looking at your actual data, almost all 75 errors are case 1 (no processed
   text). So the most useful command would be:

  ai-wiki retry     # requeue errors that have processed text, then process
  ai-wiki clear     # delete error items from the queue (clean slate for
  re-ingest)

  Want me to add both, or would you prefer just ai-wiki clear to drop the dead
  items so you can re-ingest cleanly?

❯ Add both.                                                                     
                                                                                
  Is there a `ai-wiki help` to explain the command line options? If not, add    
  that too.                                                                     
                                                                                
  And add `ai-wiki <verb> help` to give an explanation of that <verb> and to    
  list the options for that <verb>.

          +dftotext, or OCR. Books (with\n    \

     ...
      120          Commands::Ingest { path } => ingest::run(&config, &pat
           h),
      121          Commands::Tui => tui::run(&config),
      122          Commands::Process => process::run(&config),
      123 +        Commands::Retry => retry(&config),                    
      124 +        Commands::Clear => clear(&config),

      127 +                                                              
      128 +fn retry(config: &ai_wiki_core::config::Config) -> anyhow::Res
          +ult<()> {                                                     
      129 +    let queue = ai_wiki_core::queue::Queue::open(&config.paths
          +.database_path)?;                                             
      130 +                                                              
      131 +    let error_items = queue.list_items(Some(&ai_wiki_core::que
          +ue::ItemStatus::Error))?;                                     
      132 +    if error_items.is_empty() {                               
      133 +        println!("No errored items to retry.");               
      134 +        return Ok(());                                        
      135 +    }                                                         
      136 +                                                              
      137 +    let mut retried = 0usize;                                 
      138 +    let mut skipped = 0usize;                                 
      139 +                                                              
      140 +    for item in &error_items {                                
      141 +        let processed_path = config.paths.processed_dir.join(f
          +ormat!("{}.txt", item.id));                                   
      142 +        if processed_path.exists() {                          
      143 +            queue.requeue_item(item.id)?;                     
      144 +            retried += 1;                                     
      145 +        } else {                                              
      146 +            skipped += 1;                                     
      147 +        }                                                     
      148 +    }                                                         
      149 +                                                              
      150 +    println!(                                                 
      151 +        "Retry: {retried} item(s) requeued, {skipped} skipped 
          +(no processed text)."                                         
      152 +    );                                                        
      153 +                                                              
      154 +    if retried > 0 {                                          
      155 +        println!("Running process to build wiki pages...");   
      156 +        println!();                                           
      157 +        process::run(config)?;                                
      158 +    }                                                         
      159 +                                                              
      160 +    Ok(())                                                    
      161 +}                                                             
      162 +                                                              
      163 +fn clear(config: &ai_wiki_core::config::Config) -> anyhow::Res
          +ult<()> {                                                     
      164 +    let queue = ai_wiki_core::queue::Queue::open(&config.paths
          +.database_path)?;                                             
      165 +                                                              
      166 +    let error_items = queue.list_items(Some(&ai_wiki_core::que
          +ue::ItemStatus::Error))?;                                     
      167 +    if error_items.is_empty() {                               
      168 +        println!("No errored items to clear.");               
      169 +        return Ok(());                                        
      170 +    }                                                         
      171 +                                                              
      172 +    let count = error_items.len();                            
      173 +                                                              
      174 +    // Delete error items from the database                   
      175 +    let deleted = queue.delete_errors()?;                     
      176 +                                                              
      177 +    println!("Cleared {deleted} errored item(s) from the queue
          +.");                                                          
      178 +    if deleted != count as u64 {                              
      179 +        println!("  (expected {count}, deleted {deleted})");  
      180 +    }                                                         
      181 +    println!("You can now re-ingest the original files:");    
      182 +    println!("  ai-wiki ingest <path>");                      
      183 +                                                              
      184 +    Ok(())                                                    
      185 +}

      297 +    /// Delete all items with status `Error` from the queue.  
      298 +    pub fn delete_errors(&self) -> Result<u64, QueueError> {  
      299 +        // First delete children of error parents, then delete
          + the error items themselves                                   
      300 +        let child_rows = self.conn.execute(                   
      301 +            "DELETE FROM queue_items WHERE parent_id IN (SELEC
          +T id FROM queue_items WHERE status = ?1)",                    
      302 +            params![ItemStatus::Error.as_str()],              
      303 +        )?;                                                   
      304 +        let rows = self.conn.execute(                         
      305 +            "DELETE FROM queue_items WHERE status = ?1",      
      306 +            params![ItemStatus::Error.as_str()],              
      307 +        )?;                                                   
      308 +        Ok((child_rows + rows) as u64)                        
      309 +    }

✻ Crunched for 40s

❯ How can we address this variety of common error?                              
  ```                                                                           
  thread 'main' (6256771) panicked at /Users/hughbrown/.cargo/registry/src/inde 
  x.crates.io-1949cf8c6b5b557f/cff-parser-0.1.0/src/encoding.rs:150:37:         
  explicit panic                                                                
  pdf-extract panicked for /Users/hughbrown/workspace/hughdbrown/rust/ai-wiki/r 
  aw/pdf_1421_chapters/9781836200079-LLM_ENGINEERS_HANDBOOK_chapter_001.pdf     
  (likely malformed font data), falling back to pdftotext                       
  ```                                                                           
  What is malformed font data? Where does it come from? How can we fix it?      

⏺ The panic comes from the cff-parser crate (a dependency of pdf-extract). CFF
  stands for Compact Font Format — it's how fonts are embedded inside PDFs. When
   a PDF has a font with unusual or non-standard encoding tables, cff-parser
  hits an unhandled case and panics instead of returning an error.

  Where it comes from: The PDF publisher (Packt, in most of your files) embedded
   fonts that use encoding entries the parser doesn't expect. This is common
  with commercial/DRM'd PDFs, fonts with custom glyph mappings, or PDFs
  generated by certain tools (InDesign, LaTeX with exotic fonts).

  Why it's not really "malformed": The fonts work fine in every PDF reader. The
  cff-parser crate just has incomplete coverage of the CFF spec — it panics on
  valid-but-uncommon encoding entries rather than gracefully skipping them.

  Current state: We already wrap pdf_extract::extract_text in catch_unwind so
  the panic is caught and we fall back to pdftotext. The message you're seeing
  is the fallback working correctly — it's a warning, not a failure. The text
  still gets extracted via pdftotext.

  Options to reduce the noise:

  1. Downgrade the message from a warning to debug — since the fallback works,
  the user doesn't need to see it
  2. Try pdftotext first — since it handles these PDFs fine and doesn't panic,
  skip the panic-prone path entirely
  3. Skip pdf-extract for chapter files — chapters come from qpdf splits which
  pdftotext handles reliably

  I'd recommend option 2: try pdftotext first (it's fast and reliable), fall
  back to pdf-extract only if pdftotext isn't installed or returns empty text,
  then OCR as last resort. This avoids the panic entirely for the common case.
  Want me to make that change?

✻ Cooked for 1m 33s

❯ Hmmm. I guess that happens when I run roborev while instructing claude        
  directly in a differnt terminal window.                                       

⏺ Yes, exactly. When you have multiple Claude Code sessions modifying the same
  files simultaneously — one running roborev, another with direct instructions —
   the IDE's language server (rust-analyzer) gets confused. It sees partial
  writes from one session while the other is mid-edit, and reports errors on
  states that no longer exist by the time you read them.

  The compiler (cargo check) always reads the actual files from disk, so it's
  authoritative. The diagnostics in the system reminders are from
  rust-analyzer's in-memory view, which can lag behind.

  Rule of thumb: if I see diagnostics that look wrong, I run cargo check to
  verify before acting on them. That's what I've been doing throughout this
  session — and many times the "errors" turned out to be stale.

✻ Crunched for 2m 6s

❯ Modify the config file structure so that it allows there to be multiple       
  wikis.                                                                        
  Modify commands so that:                                                      
  - if there is a wiki in the current directory, no argument is needed to       
  specify the wiki (using the current directory's wiki) and                     
  - if there is no wiki, then a command line argument is needed to specify      
  which wiki is being used.                                                     
                                                                                
  Change the MCP server so that is supports multiple wikis.                     

⏺ Skill(superpowers:brainstorming)
  ⎿  Successfully loaded skill

⏺ This is a meaningful architectural change — let me think through it properly
  before coding.

  The current system has one config, one database, one wiki per project
  directory. You want multiple wikis, with automatic detection when you're in
  one.

  First clarifying question:

  Where should the registry of wikis live?

  - A) User-level config (~/.config/ai-wiki/wikis.toml) — a central registry
  listing all wikis by name and path. ai-wiki init registers the new wiki here.
  Commands check CWD against registered wiki paths, or accept --wiki <name>.
  - B) Each wiki is self-contained — no central registry. Each wiki directory
  has its own ai-wiki.toml. Commands auto-detect by walking up from CWD looking
  for ai-wiki.toml (like how git finds .git/). If not found, you pass --config 
  /path/to/ai-wiki.toml.
  - C) Central config with named wikis — a single ~/.config/ai-wiki/config.toml
  that has [wikis.rust], [wikis.python], etc. All commands take --wiki rust or
  auto-detect from CWD.

  I'd recommend B — it's the simplest, requires no central state, and follows
  the git pattern that developers already understand. Each wiki is independent.
  The MCP server would accept a --wiki-dirs argument listing paths to serve.

  What's your preference?

❯ There should be a single config file for the application in                   
  `~/.ai-wiki/config.toml`. The configuration for all wikis should be in this   
  file.                                                                         
  This is closest to your options C.                                            

⏺ Good. Next question:

  How should wikis be named and referenced?

  When you run ai-wiki ingest --wiki rust ~/Downloads/*.pdf, the rust part needs
   to map to a wiki in ~/.ai-wiki/config.toml. How should this work?

  - A) User-chosen names — ai-wiki init asks for a name (or takes --name rust).
  The config looks like:
  [wikis.rust]
  root = "/Users/hughbrown/wikis/rust"

  [wikis.python]
  root = "/Users/hughbrown/wikis/python"
  - B) Directory-based names — ai-wiki init uses the current directory name as
  the wiki name automatically. ai-wiki init in /Users/hughbrown/wikis/rust
  creates a wiki named rust.
  - C) Both — defaults to the directory name but accepts --name to override.

  I'd recommend C — sensible default, override when needed.

❯ option C                                                                      
⏺ Next question:

  What should auto-detection look for when you're inside a wiki directory?

  When you run ai-wiki ingest file.pdf without --wiki, the tool needs to figure
  out which wiki you mean. Options:

  - A) Match CWD against registered wiki roots — check if CWD equals or is under
   any wiki's root path from ~/.ai-wiki/config.toml. Fast, no filesystem
  walking.
  - B) Walk up looking for a marker file — look for ai-wiki.toml in CWD, then
  parent, etc. (git-style). But this conflicts with the central config approach.
  - C) Match CWD, fail with a helpful list if ambiguous — option A, but if no
  match is found, print all registered wikis and ask the user to specify --wiki 
  <name>.

  I'd recommend A with C's error handling — match CWD against registered roots,
  and if no match, print the available wikis.

  Does that work?

❯ Option A                                                                      

⏺ Next question:

  What goes in each wiki's root directory vs. the central config?

  Currently ai-wiki.toml has paths, PDF settings, rejection patterns, and tool
  paths. With multiple wikis, some of these are per-wiki and some are global.
  Proposed split:

  Global (in ~/.ai-wiki/config.toml):
  - Tool paths (qpdf, pdftotext, tesseract, ffmpeg, whisper-cpp)
  - These are system-level, same for all wikis

  Per-wiki (under [wikis.<name>]):
  - root — the wiki directory (contains wiki/, processed/, raw/, ai-wiki.db)
  - PDF settings (book_min_pages)
  - Rejection patterns (non_operative_extensions, sensitive_filename_patterns)

  So the config would look like:

  [tools]
  qpdf_path = "qpdf"
  pdftotext_path = "pdftotext"
  pdftoppm_path = "pdftoppm"
  tesseract_path = "tesseract"
  ffmpeg_path = "ffmpeg"
  whisper_cpp_path = "whisper-cpp"
  whisper_model_path = "models/ggml-large-v3.bin"

  [wikis.rust]
  root = "/Users/hughbrown/wikis/rust"
  book_min_pages = 50
  non_operative_extensions = [".dmg"]
  sensitive_filename_patterns = ["divorce", "court", "financial"]

  [wikis.python]
  root = "/Users/hughbrown/wikis/python"
  book_min_pages = 50
  non_operative_extensions = [".dmg"]
  sensitive_filename_patterns = ["divorce", "court", "financial"]

  Each wiki's root directory contains the fixed subdirectory structure: wiki/,
  processed/, raw/, ai-wiki.db.

  Does this split look right, or should per-wiki settings inherit defaults to
  avoid repeating rejection patterns everywhere?

❯ Mostly right.                                                                 
  There should now be no `sensitive_filename_patterns`. I initially said that   
  when I was making a technical wiki and I was selecting files from a directory 
   that had lots of files dumped into it. But now I want to create wikis that   
  use such files (although still not in the technical wiki) and I want to relax 
   this earlier restriction.                                                    
                                                                                
  So remove that condition. Similarly, the `non_operative_extensions` is not    
  needed. The loader will know how to load files of particular types and will   
  only enqueue suitable ones.                                                   

⏺ Good — that simplifies things. So rejection is just file-type detection (the
  code already handles this — unknown extensions get rejected). No configurable
  patterns needed.

  The config becomes:

  [tools]
  qpdf_path = "qpdf"
  pdftotext_path = "pdftotext"
  pdftoppm_path = "pdftoppm"
  tesseract_path = "tesseract"
  ffmpeg_path = "ffmpeg"
  whisper_cpp_path = "whisper-cpp"
  whisper_model_path = "models/ggml-large-v3.bin"

  [wikis.rust]
  root = "/Users/hughbrown/wikis/rust"
  book_min_pages = 50

  [wikis.python]
  root = "/Users/hughbrown/wikis/python"
  book_min_pages = 50

  And each wiki's root has:
  rust/
  ├── wiki/          (Obsidian vault)
  ├── processed/     (extracted text)
  ├── raw/           (split PDFs, extracted ZIPs)
  └── ai-wiki.db     (SQLite queue)

  Next question:

  For the MCP server, how should it handle multiple wikis?

  - A) One MCP server instance serving all wikis — reads ~/.ai-wiki/config.toml,
   exposes tools with a wiki_name parameter on each call (e.g.,
  get_next_item(wiki: "rust")). One process, one registration with Claude Code.
  - B) One MCP server instance per wiki — register multiple times: claude mcp 
  add ai-wiki-rust -- ai-wiki-mcp --wiki rust. Each instance serves one wiki.
  Simple tools (no wiki parameter needed).

  I'd recommend A — one process, less overhead, Claude can work across wikis in
  a single session. The wiki parameter is a small addition to each tool call.

❯ I think we register a single MCP server and the name of the wiki (looked up   
  in the configuration file) becomes mandatory.                                 

⏺ Agreed. Every MCP tool call requires a wiki parameter. No default, no
  auto-detect — the LLM must always specify which wiki it's operating on.

  Let me present the design. I'll go section by section.

  Section 1: Config Structure

  File: ~/.ai-wiki/config.toml

  [tools]
  qpdf_path = "qpdf"
  pdftotext_path = "pdftotext"
  pdftoppm_path = "pdftoppm"
  tesseract_path = "tesseract"
  ffmpeg_path = "ffmpeg"
  whisper_cpp_path = "whisper-cpp"
  whisper_model_path = "models/ggml-large-v3.bin"

  [wikis.rust]
  root = "/Users/hughbrown/wikis/rust"
  book_min_pages = 50

  [wikis.python]
  root = "/Users/hughbrown/wikis/python"
  book_min_pages = 30

  Each wiki's root contains: wiki/, processed/, raw/, ai-wiki.db — these paths
  are derived from root, not configured individually.

  The old per-project ai-wiki.toml goes away entirely. Everything lives in
  ~/.ai-wiki/config.toml.

  Does this section look right?

❯ Just one thing -- I don't know what `book_min_pages` is for. What does that   
  do?                                                                           

⏺ It controls when a PDF gets split into chapters vs. ingested whole.

  When you ingest a PDF, the code checks: does it have a table of contents
  (outlines) AND is it longer than book_min_pages? If both are true, it's
  classified as a "Book" and split into separate chapter files via qpdf.
  Otherwise it's treated as a "Simple" PDF and ingested as a single file.

  The default is 50 pages. So a 200-page book with a TOC gets split into
  chapters, but a 10-page article with a TOC doesn't.

  You might want different thresholds for different wikis — a wiki of academic
  papers might set it higher (100) so short papers with outlines aren't split,
  while a wiki of textbooks might keep it at 50.

  That said, if you've never needed to change it from the default, it could just
   be a global setting under [tools] instead of per-wiki. Or removed entirely
  and hardcoded.

  Want to:
  - A) Keep it per-wiki (some wikis have different source material)
  - B) Move it to global [tools] section
  - C) Hardcode it at 50 and remove the config option

❯ I think that any document that has a table of contents gets split, regardless 
   of length.                                                                   
  Are there 10 page articles with TOCs? Have you seen one? That would be weird, 
   because TOC is to help with navigation, but a 10-page PDF has no real        
  navigation problem.                                                           

⏺ You're right. A PDF with a TOC is a book. A 10-page PDF with a real TOC would
  be unusual — and even if it exists, splitting it into chapters is harmless.
  The chapters would just be short.

  So: remove book_min_pages entirely. If a PDF has a TOC (level-1 outlines),
  split it. If not, ingest whole.

  The config simplifies to:

  [tools]
  qpdf_path = "qpdf"
  pdftotext_path = "pdftotext"
  pdftoppm_path = "pdftoppm"
  tesseract_path = "tesseract"
  ffmpeg_path = "ffmpeg"
  whisper_cpp_path = "whisper-cpp"
  whisper_model_path = "models/ggml-large-v3.bin"

  [wikis.rust]
  root = "/Users/hughbrown/wikis/rust"

  [wikis.python]
  root = "/Users/hughbrown/wikis/python"

  Each wiki entry is just a name and a root path. Clean.

  Does this look right to proceed?

❯ I think that is right.                                                        

⏺ Section 2: CLI Commands

  All commands read ~/.ai-wiki/config.toml. Wiki is determined by:
  1. Check if CWD is at or under any registered wiki's root — if so, use that
  wiki
  2. Otherwise, require --wiki <name> flag
  3. If neither, print available wikis and exit with error

  ai-wiki init [--name <name>] [<directory>]
      # Creates wiki in <directory> (default: CWD)
      # Name defaults to directory name
      # Registers in ~/.ai-wiki/config.toml

  ai-wiki ingest [--wiki <name>] <path>
  ai-wiki process [--wiki <name>]
  ai-wiki tui [--wiki <name>]
  ai-wiki retry [--wiki <name>]
  ai-wiki clear [--wiki <name>]
  ai-wiki queue [--wiki <name>] {claim|complete|error}

  The --config flag goes away — config is always ~/.ai-wiki/config.toml.

  One new command:

  ai-wiki list
      # Lists all registered wikis with name, root path, and item counts

  Does this look right?

❯ The `Wiki is determined by:` test is backwards, in my view.                   
  If the command specifies a wiki and the name used does not match a wiki in    
  the current directory, the `name` should be used.                             
  If the user insists on specifying a name, use the name.                       

⏺ You're right. The --wiki flag takes priority:

  1. If --wiki <name> is specified, use that wiki — regardless of CWD
  2. If no --wiki, check if CWD is at or under a registered wiki's root — if so,
   use that wiki
  3. If neither, print available wikis and exit with error

  The user's explicit choice always wins.

  Does this look right?

❯ Yes. Begin implementation.

      111  ## Usage
      112  
      120 -ai-wiki operates in two phases: **load** and **process**.     
      113 +### Wiki Selection                                            
      114  
      115 +When you're inside a wiki's directory, commands auto-detect wh
          +ich wiki to use:                                              
      116 +```bash                                                       
      117 +cd ~/wikis/rust                                               
      118 +ai-wiki ingest ~/Downloads/rust-book.pdf    # uses the "rust" 
          +wiki                                                          
      119 +```                                                           
      120 +                                                              
      121 +From anywhere else, specify the wiki by name:                 
      122 +```bash                                                       
      123 +ai-wiki --wiki rust ingest ~/Downloads/rust-book.pdf          
      124 +```                                                           
      125 +                                                              
      126 +The `--wiki` flag always takes priority over directory detecti
          +on.                                                           
      127 +                                                              
      128  ### Phase 1: Load (Ingest)
      129  
      124 -Ingest reads your source files, classifies them, extracts text
          -, and queues them for LLM processing. No LLM is involved in th
          -is phase -- it's pure Rust.                                   
      130 +Ingest reads source files, classifies them, extracts text, and
          + queues them for LLM processing. No LLM is involved -- pure Ru
          +st preprocessing.                                             
      131  
      132  ```bash
      127 -# Ingest a single file                                        
      133  ai-wiki ingest ~/Downloads/paper.pdf
      129 -                                                              
      130 -# Ingest a directory                                          
      134  ai-wiki ingest ~/Downloads/rust-books/
      132 -                                                              
      133 -# Ingest with a glob pattern (quotes prevent shell expansion; 
          -ai-wiki expands globs internally)                             
      135  ai-wiki ingest "~/Downloads/*.pdf"
      135 -                                                              
      136 -# Ingest from a file list (one path per line, # comments allow
          -ed)                                                           
      136  ai-wiki ingest @my-reading-list.txt
      137  ```
      138  
      139  What happens during ingest:
      140  
      142 -- **Markdown/text files** are copied to the processed director
          -y as-is.                                                      
      143 -- **PDFs** are classified:                                    
      144 -  - Simple PDFs: text is extracted (pdf-extract, pdftotext, or
          - OCR as fallback).                                            
      145 -  - Books (outlines + 50+ pages): split into chapters via `qpd
          -f`, each chapter extracted separately.                        
      146 -  - Sensitive files (matching rejection patterns): rejected an
          -d logged.                                                     
      147 -- **ZIP files** are extracted and each contained file is proce
          -ssed recursively.                                             
      148 -- **Audio/video** (MP4, MKV, etc.): audio extracted with ffmpe
          -g, transcribed with whisper-cpp.                              
      149 -- **Non-operative files** (.dmg, etc.): rejected immediately. 
      141 +- **PDFs** with a table of contents are split into chapters vi
          +a `qpdf`. Text extracted via pdf-extract, pdftotext, or OCR (p
          +dftoppm + tesseract).                                         
      142 +- **Markdown/text** files are copied directly.                
      143 +- **ZIP** archives are extracted and each file processed recur
          +sively.                                                       
      144 +- **Audio/video** (MP4, MKV, etc.) are transcribed via ffmpeg 
          ++ whisper-cpp.                                                
      145 +- **Unknown file types** are rejected.                        
      146  
      151 -Each file gets a queue entry in SQLite. Duplicate files are de
          -tected and skipped automatically.                             
      152 -                                                              
      153 -Progress is shown for each file:                              
      147 +Duplicate files are detected and skipped automatically. Progre
          +ss is shown per file:                                         
      148  ```
      149  [1/794] document.pdf ... queued (0.3s)
      150  [2/794] installer.dmg ... rejected (0.0s)
      151  [3/794] already-done.pdf ... skipped (0.0s)
      158 -Ingest complete — queued: 500, rejected: 12, errors: 3, skippe
          -d: 279, failed: 0 (4m 23s)                                    
      152 +Ingest complete — queued: 500, rejected: 12, errors: 3, skippe
          +d: 279 (4m 23s)                                               
      153  ```
      154  
      155  ### Phase 2: Process (LLM)
      156  
      163 -Processing invokes Claude to read the extracted text and build
          - wiki pages.                                                  
      164 -                                                              
      165 -> **Security note:** The `process` command runs Claude with br
          -oad tool access (`--dangerously-skip-permissions`). Only proce
          -ss documents you trust, as source content could potentially tr
          -igger unintended actions via prompt injection.                
      166 -                                                              
      157  ```bash
      158  ai-wiki process
      159  ```
      160  
      171 -This processes all queued items. For each item, Claude:       
      172 -1. Reads the extracted text                                   
      173 -2. Identifies entities, concepts, and claims                  
      174 -3. Creates wiki pages with YAML frontmatter and `[[wikilinks]]
          -`                                                             
      175 -4. Updates the index and log                                  
      176 -5. Marks the item complete                                    
      161 +Invokes Claude to read each queued item's extracted text, crea
          +te wiki pages with YAML frontmatter and `[[wikilinks]]`, updat
          +e the index and log, and mark items complete.                 
      162  
      178 -The wiki follows Obsidian conventions:                        
      179 -- `entities/` -- people, organizations, tools                 
      180 -- `concepts/` -- ideas, theories, techniques                  
      181 -- `claims/` -- specific assertions with `data-point: true` tag
      182 -- `sources/` -- summaries of ingested documents               
      183 -- `index.md` -- catalog of all pages

      185 -- `CLAUDE.md` -- schema telling the LLM how to maintain the wi
          -ki                                                            
      163 +> **Security note:** The `process` command grants Claude broad
          + tool access. Only process documents you trust.

      223 +- `complete_item(wiki, id, wiki_page_path)` — mark item comple
          +te                                                            
      224 +- `read_source(wiki, id)` — read extracted text               
      225 +- `read_page(wiki, path)` — read a wiki page                  
      226 +- `write_page(wiki, path, content)` — create/update a wiki pag
          +e                                                             
      227 +- `list_pages(wiki, directory)` — list pages                  
      228 +- `read_index(wiki)` — read index.md                          
      229 +- `update_index(wiki, entry)` — append to index               
      230 +- `append_log(wiki, entry)` — append to log                   
      231  
      243 -```bash                                                       
      244 -cargo run -p pdf-dump -- ~/Downloads/some-book.pdf            
      245 -```                                                           
      232 +### Cross-Wiki Queries                                        
      233  
      247 -Output shows:                                                 
      248 -1. **Table of contents** -- all outline entries with nesting l
          -evel and page number                                          
      249 -2. **Split blocks** -- how the book would be divided into chap
          -ters (top-level entries only, with start/end page numbers)    
      250 -3. **Comparison** -- flags if the current splitting code would
          - over-fragment the book by using sub-sections instead of just 
          -top-level entries                                             
      251 -

      252  ## Project Structure
      253  
      254  ```
      255  ai-wiki/
      256  ├── crates/
      281 -│   ├── ai-wiki-core/     # Library: config, queue, preprocess
          -ing, wiki operations                                          
      282 -│   ├── ai-wiki/          # CLI binary: ingest, tui, process  
      283 -│   ├── ai-wiki-mcp/      # MCP server: 11 tools for Claude Co
          -de integration                                                
      284 -│   └── pdf-dump/         # Diagnostic utility for PDF inspect
          -ion                                                           
      257 +│   ├── ai-wiki-core/     # Library: config, queue, preprocess
          +ing, wiki                                                     
      258 +│   ├── ai-wiki/          # CLI: init, ingest, process, tui, r
          +etry, clear, list, queue                                      
      259 +│   ├── ai-wiki-mcp/      # MCP server: multi-wiki, 12 tools  
      260 +│   └── pdf-dump/         # PDF chapter inspection utility    
      261  ├── docs/
      286 -│   ├── design/           # Original design documents         
      287 -│   └── superpowers/      # Implementation plans and review fi
          -ndings                                                        
      288 -├── wiki/                 # Generated Obsidian vault (gitignor
          -ed content)                                                   
      289 -├── processed/            # Extracted text files (gitignored) 
      290 -├── raw/                  # Split PDFs and extracted ZIPs (git
          -ignored)                                                      
      291 -├── ai-wiki.toml          # Configuration                     
      292 -├── justfile              # Task runner recipes               
      262 +│   ├── design/           # Design documents                  
      263 +│   └── superpowers/      # Specs, plans, reviews             
      264 +├── justfile              # Task runner                       
      265  └── README.md
      266 +                                                              
      267 +~/.ai-wiki/                                                   
      268 +└── config.toml           # Central config with tool paths and
          + wiki registry                                                
      269  ```

⏺ Bash(git add -A && git commit -m "$(cat <<'EOF'
      docs: update README for multi-wiki support, add querying guide…)
  ⎿  [main 8fa70de] docs: update README for multi-wiki support, add queryin
     g guide
      10 files changed, 1100 insertions(+), 215 deletions(-)
     … +4 lines (ctrl+o to expand)

⏺ Multi-wiki support is implemented. Here's a summary of what changed:

  Config: ~/.ai-wiki/config.toml replaces per-project ai-wiki.toml. Global
  [tools] section + [wikis.<name>] entries with just a root path each.

  CLI:
  - --config removed, --wiki <name> added
  - ai-wiki init [--name <name>] [<dir>] creates and registers a wiki
  - ai-wiki list shows all wikis
  - All commands auto-detect wiki from CWD, or accept --wiki

  Removed: book_min_pages (any PDF with TOC gets split),
  sensitive_filename_patterns, non_operative_extensions, PdfConfig,
  RejectionConfig

  MCP Server: Holds AppConfig, every tool call requires wiki parameter. Single
  server instance serves all wikis.

  README: Updated with multi-wiki workflow, querying guide (direct + MCP),
  cross-wiki examples.

✻ Churned for 20m 5s

❯ /usage 
  ⎿  Status dialog dismissed
